    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3583561297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3583561297" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3583561297?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=mystery-detective-thriller">mystery-detective-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=nordic-noir">nordic-noir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3583561297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10884919715240206528">Someone is Killing the Police!<br/><br/>Police is the second mega-volume of what I said I suspected to be Jo Nesbo’s magnum opus, the pinnacle of his literary accomplishments, after the cliffhanger of Phantom, when it appears Harry Hole is shot and killed. But then there’s another volume, so, well, hey, maybe he’s not dead, kids! <br/><br/>And for ⅓ of Police we are supposedly in suspense about this issue, and are left with the rest of the nice and interesting (but not particuarly brilliant) group of Harry’s poice </span>
  <span id="freeText10884919715240206528" style="display:none">Someone is Killing the Police!<br /><br />Police is the second mega-volume of what I said I suspected to be Jo Nesbo’s magnum opus, the pinnacle of his literary accomplishments, after the cliffhanger of Phantom, when it appears Harry Hole is shot and killed. But then there’s another volume, so, well, hey, maybe he’s not dead, kids! <br /><br />And for ⅓ of Police we are supposedly in suspense about this issue, and are left with the rest of the nice and interesting (but not particuarly brilliant) group of Harry’s poice colleagues to try to keep Oslo safe. I mean, we like Beata and Katrina and they desreve their time at center stage, but it's just kicking the can down the road til--hey, presto!--Harry returns to Save the Day. But one of the things I liked about Phantom was that it is not one of his serial killer books, that it focused on Harry’s relationship to Oleg, and Harry's attempt to free Oleg from jail and exonerate him. But alas--for me, not a fan of serial killer books and especially not the increasingly brutal ways Nesbo does it--we discover that a particularly vicious serial killer is killing the police, and/or their families.<br /><br />So I thought it was all technically well done, as usual, this combination of thriller/mystery Nesbo accomplishes that involves twists and turns and surprises along the way that are carefully planned. And yes, the fact that the first ⅓ has us get to knowHarrry’s friends/colleagues better figures in to the fact that one of them we have come to know and care about actually dies. I get the point of that. And I like the way the concept of a “burner”--an insider in the police force who is corrupted to foil police investigations--works out in the end of Police. And I like it that the book ends with a kind of catharsis, a family moment.<br /><br />And I am interested in the way Nesbo explores the typical mystery trope of Killer as Madman. Some of Harry’s colleagues are identified with various psychological conditions and neurological disorders--Asperger’s Syndrome, Bi-Polar. Harry himself sees that he is himself psychologically addicted to solving police cases as much as he is to alcohol. And yet he and his friends accomplish much with their disabilities. But then there is the serial killer, a phenomenon Nesbo has researched in depth. I know, this is supposed to be sensational centerpiece of the story, but it is so over-the-top sadistic at times you can't take it seriously. And then there is a student who hits on Harry who says he is probably schizophrenic? Not convincing in any real way, that episode.<br /><br />The book begins very slowly, and then each killing has to be unique and shocking, but it has a kind of forgettable sameness to it that leaves soon after you are--I admit it--griped in the fever of the moment. And I have to say, I have never been interested in the least in the inter-office or Oslo city politics. Mikael Bellman, the Alpha-male wanna-be Chief of Police, is never real to me, just a cartoon character, such as Goldfinger. And the woman Bellman has a dalliance with from the City Council--also a cartoon character, like Pussy Galore. But it is well done, and I was pretty engaged, the twists are well done. Considered as one of a genre, a thriller, this is superior work, and I listened to it all the way through as quickly as possible. That’s what a thriller should do, I guess. 3.5ish, for my tastes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10884919715240206528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1133170001" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1133170001" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133170001?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133170001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7528525709221707222">Nesbø brings the Harry Hole series to a close with a thriller that keeps readers focussed until the final sentence. After the vague, yet horrible, end to the previous novel, the complete cast of characters remains in shock about how the Oslo Crime Squad will continue. When a number of police officers are murdered after returned to crime scenes of previously unsolved cases, there's a struggle between the Squad and Kripos (the national police organisation) as to who will handle things. Newly-appoi</span>
  <span id="freeText7528525709221707222" style="display:none">Nesbø brings the Harry Hole series to a close with a thriller that keeps readers focussed until the final sentence. After the vague, yet horrible, end to the previous novel, the complete cast of characters remains in shock about how the Oslo Crime Squad will continue. When a number of police officers are murdered after returned to crime scenes of previously unsolved cases, there's a struggle between the Squad and Kripos (the national police organisation) as to who will handle things. Newly-appointed Chief of Police, Mikael Bellman, defers to the national authorities, though does permit a loose collection of Squad members to run a covert investigation. Leaderless now, with Hole's seat empty, the team tries to piece things together, with little success. Lingering over them is the Gusto Hanssen case, crux of the previous novel, which remains unsolved, though many feel Hole knew how it all came together. Some key players in the scheme, from criminals through to Bellman and his lackey, remain on high alert, as their futures could hang in the balance if such news were shared. As the Squad limps along, trying to solve the police murder, they face a devastating reality, and are hit with tragedy. At this point, they can no longer work alone. Harry Hole, now a full-time instructor at the Police Academy, is called upon to help as a consultant. Hole is tepid in his acceptance, but needs a distraction as he is badgered by an overly flirtatious student who cries wolf when things do not go her way. Hole works as best he can and traces down a few leads, with a focus on the killer from the original crimes, most of whom have a strong sexual component to them. Alibis preclude an easy arrest and the Squad is forced to return to the drawing board, with little to show for their work. As Hole is wont to do, he finds a thread and pulls, which causes everything to unravel to its bare basics and offers new insights that the Squad had not seen beforehand. With a Cop Killer on the loose, other storylines also ramp up, leaving the reader to split their interest along a few developing narratives. With nothing to lose, will Hole end his time as Nesbø's protagonist on a winning note, or will the Crime Squad disappear onto the literary horizon with more unanswered questions and force readers to extrapolate on their own? Brilliant work, told in such a way that no Nesbø fan could complain.<br /><br />Nesbø is a master at picking up where he leaves off, not always letting the reader breathe before pushing the drama that ended the previous novel into the forefront. His insinuations, at multiple points in the book, leave the reader to wonder what if rather than knowing how things will play out. Nesbø's use of a sizeable character base allows multiple plots to develop without straining realistic expectations of those he uses as vessels to guide the narrative. Harry Hole may be central, but Nesbø shows how the story can progress without him, at least for a period, while installing fear and loathing in the reader. That the series had to come to an end is inevitable, though Harry Hole had an excellent run. With new and disturbing addictions or dark pathways, Hole remains a man with a number of struggles for which he has not found an answer. This ever-evolving character exemplifies how Nesbø is able to hold onto his 'Master of the Art' title without much opposition by readers.<br /><br />When I began this Harry Hole journey, I was not sure what to expect. On the one hand, I love a good police procedural, particularly one that takes place outside of the normal 'North American' or 'British-centric' locales that many of the novels I have read find themselves developing. On the other, there is always a gamble to be taken when reading a collection of novels that were written in a language other than English. The translator must be stellar, as they represent the author's ideas. As my Norwegian is as rusty as it could ever be, I relied on a translation and the hype Harry Hole had received to see if things could develop into an addictive for me. Like Harry Hole and bottle of Jim Beam, they did and I was ensconced in the series from the early stages. While it took three books to pull the story into Norway, once things got moving, there was no end to the wonders Nesbø placed before the reader. That Hole is an effective detective is even more surprising, based on the addictions and dark side he undertakes throughout the series. As I have mentioned at numerous points in past reviews, the alcoholism and drug abuse seem only to heighten Hole's abilities, while pulling the reader into the dark world of drugs on Oslo's streets. With a successful trilogy built into the larger series, Nesbø keeps the reader hooked and wanting more. Hole's ongoing love interests seem to flit across the page, though Rakel's emergence with her son Oleg remain a storyline that Nesbø does not end and Hole relies upon, no matter what he is doing. I cannot say enough about this series, this author, or the fact that Scandinavian crime novels seem better than much of the genre that is written in English at the outset.<br /><br />Kudos Mr. Nesbø for a powerful piece to end the series. I have found a new favourite author and will recommend this series to anyone who will listen.<br /><br />Like/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7528525709221707222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_665413381" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/665413381" />
    <a title="donna_ehm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17628565-donna-ehm"><img alt="donna_ehm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361498784p2/17628565.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/665413381?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="donna_ehm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="donna_ehm" href="/user/show/17628565-donna-ehm">donna_ehm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846555961" href="/book/show/16134936-police">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer665413381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16857408498320186220">I hemmed and hawed over a 2 or 3 star rating, then eventually decided the excellent <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[fake out at the end <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> deserved the third star. <br/><br/>Overall, this book showcases Nesbo's ability to manipulate multiple storylines and characters such that you're always kept guessing as to how it's all going to turn out. This time, though, I felt that the plot was wobbly around the edges, like he didn't quite have as firm a hold on those threads as he usually does. Some things I just didn</span>
  <span id="freeText16857408498320186220" style="display:none">I hemmed and hawed over a 2 or 3 star rating, then eventually decided the excellent <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[fake out at the end <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> deserved the third star. <br /><br />Overall, this book showcases Nesbo's ability to manipulate multiple storylines and characters such that you're always kept guessing as to how it's all going to turn out. This time, though, I felt that the plot was wobbly around the edges, like he didn't quite have as firm a hold on those threads as he usually does. Some things I just didn't buy, like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Trul's remarkable recovery from essentially having his head and face smashed to bits. I didn't believe for one second that he could be up and around with seemingly only the physical scars/damage to show for it, rather than the extreme brain damage you'd fully expect, given how the murderer treated his previous victims. And in this case, the murderer didn't intend to leave Truls alive, so there's no reason to think that the violence would be any less thorough or complete.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Also, I think the entire sub-plot with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the academy student who has a crush on Harry <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> could have been dropped entirely. I thought it was completely unnecessary, and it's only real purpose (beyond being a bit of a red herring for the reader) was to provide yet another level for Harry to sink to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, i.e. a potential rapist. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Those scenes really annoyed me, to be honest, because no matter how dark and tortured Harry is, I truly don't believe that he'd <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ actually consider raping someone. It's irrelevant that the situation was described such that the sex would have been entirely consensual, because the important thing is that Harry still thought of the situation as one of rape, and he was willing to go there. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I just thought Harry didn't need yet one more thing to be tormented by, and for all his faults, this particular demon is not one of his. It just came across as titillation for its own sake, and nothing I could take seriously as part of the story. Plus the idea of it being wrapped up in <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the cliche of 'man freaks out after proposing/thinks he'll fuck everything up' was just really lame. We've been down that road with Harry many times before. He knows he wants to be with Rakel at this point. Tossing that in there in order to get the reader to think he might - yet one more time! - do something to jeopardize that was just lazy writing, I think. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The final thing that really annoyed me (and had me contemplating that two star rating) was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the death of Beate. I really, really liked her character and how she evolved into this very cool person in her own right, not to mention her great relationship with Harry. But what made her death even more frustrating was that it came across as the thing that had to be done in order to draw Harry into the investigation officially. Like, her character was sacrificed as a means to move the plot in a particular direction, and after that it didn't have any meaning or really resonate with the reader. By comparison, the death of Harry's first partner, Ellen (in <i>The Redbreast</i>) comes with a lot of emotional consequences and ramifications for Harry, not only for the rest of that book but for the next one or two that come after. So as a reader you really feel how that death not only affected the plot but also how it affected the characters. It had meaning beyond just mobilizing Harry, and that was woven into the plot itself. But Beate's death seemed much more to be just this thing, this event that happened and then the story carried on. I thought the character deserved much more than that, so that was very disappointing. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />On the upside, I was pleased that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Harry got a happy ending. He's never going to be a sunny, well-adjusted guy, we all know that and so do the characters in the novels (especially Rakel). But I think it's realistic to see him being rewarded, if you will, because he truly has been trying to turn his life around as much as he can. He knows the importance of this relationship, he knows his own weaknesses as well as his strengths, so while he'll probably always be a work in progress, he has been moving slowly forward ever since meeting Rakel. I have liked that his addictions have never been downplayed or waved away with a magic wand because that's the reality of having those addictions. But at the same time, I think the self-destructive loner cop/detective is such a cliche, so I really wanted Harry to having something positive, something real and true because I also think that's the reality for many people dealing with these types of issues. You can deal, you can make some sort of peace with who you are and what you have, you can have a good life. The reactions of Harry, Rakel and Oleg during the wedding scene felt very genuine, so I was happy to read that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There's obviously another story in the works, although this would certainly be a fitting end to the series, if Nesbo wanted to play it that way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16857408498320186220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2808464252" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2808464252" />
    <a title="Alex Cantone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48050946-alex-cantone"><img alt="Alex Cantone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479001219p2/48050946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2808464252?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex Cantone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex Cantone" href="/user/show/48050946-alex-cantone">Alex Cantone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099570097" href="/book/show/18460029-police">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48050946-alex-cantone?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48050946-alex-cantone?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48050946-alex-cantone?shelf=noir">noir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2808464252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11390888937263551820"><i>Anton looked up. He hadn’t heard the two of them coming, although they emerged from the dense thickets. He had seen it before, how forensic officers moved at crime scenes, like somewhat ungainly dancers bending and twisting, positioning their feet, as though they were astronauts on the moon. Or perhaps it was the white overalls drawing the association.</i><br/><br/><b>Police</b> revolves around a series of grisly (perhaps the French <i>macabre</i> is a better choice) murders of Oslo police detectives, each lured to the sit</span>
  <span id="freeText11390888937263551820" style="display:none"><i>Anton looked up. He hadn’t heard the two of them coming, although they emerged from the dense thickets. He had seen it before, how forensic officers moved at crime scenes, like somewhat ungainly dancers bending and twisting, positioning their feet, as though they were astronauts on the moon. Or perhaps it was the white overalls drawing the association.</i><br /><br /><b>Police</b> revolves around a series of grisly (perhaps the French <i>macabre</i> is a better choice) murders of Oslo police detectives, each lured to the site of an earlier unsolved crime. The investigation focuses on Valentin Gjertsen, a key suspect in the unsolved cases but who was given an alibi. He was presumed bludgeoned to death in Ita prison by fellow inmates, but Katrine Bratt discovers that Gjertsen “staged” his own death and escaped. However, some of the evidence doesn’t fit the pattern, and a now sober Harry Hole, lecturing at the police academy, with his small specialist team put together by Gunnar Hagen, speculates there may be two murderers at work.<br /><br />This is the 10th book in the Harry Hole series and 8th in the Oslo sequence. The events take place nearly two years after <b>Phantom</b> and despite my own tendency to browse and read at random, that book should be read before this one as several incidents relate to that and his earlier books. (How I wish I’d taken better notes at the time).<br /><br />The usual characters are here: Harry and Rakel and her son Oleg, being treated in a Swiss clinic for drug addiction. Mikael Bellman is Chief of Police and touted for a possible political career, with his loyal wife Ulla, his on/off lover Councillor Isobel Skøyen and his unloved childhood friend, Officer Truls Berntsen, on suspension for undeclared funds in his bank account. Forensic pathologists Beate Lønn and Bjørn Holm and psychologist Ståle Aune are all more fleshed out, and Katrine Bratt, formerly with the Bergen police joins the team, with her fingertips flying relentlessly over the keyboard.<br /><br /><i>Katrine said: ‘Women can’t park, they don’t remember football results and they can’t be bothered to learn the fiddly bits on computers. For that you need weird men with band T-shirts and minimal sex lives, and it’s been like this ever since the Stone Age.’</i><br /><br />By and large, if Nesbø describes a character at length they are either a villain or future victim, but the author throws in some minor characters just to set the scene.<br /><br /><i>The lack of light meant he had to ski by feeling and try to predict how the snow and the ground would roll and pitch beneath the skis. But that was his special talent, which meant he always did best when there was bad visibility, heavy snow, mist, flat light: he could feel what he couldn’t see…</i><br /><br />At 630 pages you get a big bang for your buck: a slow starter that switches between the police murders unfolding and a mystery witness in a coma in a hospital ward under police guard. Harry Hole doesn’t really put in an appearance until page 200, and from then on the author ratchets up the tension until the reader is feverishly turning the pages…at risk of missing out on an important clue.<br /><br />In between there is an obsessed police cadet and some discussion among the group, in the context of the police academy, of the terms “murder” – taken to mean premeditated, and “killing”, which could be accidental, in self-defence or in defence of a loved one, or in the line of duty of the military or police. <br /><br />Verdict: another 5 star read, which nicely sets up the next book, <b>The Thirst</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11390888937263551820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_2808464252'><a id="like_count_review_2808464252" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/2808464252?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">13 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F18142329-police">Like</a></span>

<div id="review_1066702546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1066702546" />
    <a title="Steven Belanger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3985022-steven-belanger"><img alt="Steven Belanger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473814599p2/3985022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1066702546?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steven Belanger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steven Belanger" href="/user/show/3985022-steven-belanger">Steven Belanger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1066702546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4754554825678305738">Very, very, very disappointing follow-up to Nesbo's Phantom, a far superior book, even with the ridiculous passages from the rat's POV. In equal parts boring and frustrating--but mostly frustrating--Police is a book that could've been, and should've been, much better. <br/><br/>It fails because it's all over the place with its plot and story, and because it doesn't focus enough on its characters. Nesbo said in an interview that he essentially wrote Phantom and Police as one book, and it shows. At over 1,0</span>
  <span id="freeText4754554825678305738" style="display:none">Very, very, very disappointing follow-up to Nesbo's Phantom, a far superior book, even with the ridiculous passages from the rat's POV. In equal parts boring and frustrating--but mostly frustrating--Police is a book that could've been, and should've been, much better. <br /><br />It fails because it's all over the place with its plot and story, and because it doesn't focus enough on its characters. Nesbo said in an interview that he essentially wrote Phantom and Police as one book, and it shows. At over 1,000 pages combined, it seems like Nesbo couldn't wait to finish with the ending, that even he became bored and frustrated with it.<br /><br />How else to explain the inexplicable demise of a major recurring character? How else to explain how the killer could've had the time to draw and quarter this well-liked character while on the run from everyone? Could the killer really have chopped off her arms and legs and head in (seemingly) minutes? Then stash them all in different bags and deposit them in the trash just in time for the trucks?<br /><br />What?!? And, by the way, didn't this character deserve so much better? She's rarely considered for the rest of the book--though everyone was sure not to sit in her chair--and it's never explained why she was done away with when other characters were not, even when we were tricked into thinking they would be.<br /><br />And that was another thing. Way too many cheap tricks, like making us think a character's young daughter was in danger when her father calls her friend Emilie's house to inquire about her sleepover. Turns out, she was at the sleepover after all--just at a different girl's house...another girl in the same class, also named Emilie!!! Ugh...<br /><br />Another time a character looks like she's about to get it, but it was just another character sneaking up on her. She even says that, hey, you're not John Doe--but it turns out he was. She just meant that he wasn't acting like himself. Please...<br /><br />Another time a very distraught father was acting strange at the scene of his daughter's death, just after a character in the previous section said that murders were happening by someone distraught about love, and at the death scene of those he loved. Turns out, he was actually just in grief about his daughter dying, one year to the day...Argh!<br /><br />The real bad guy is a case of who cares. The ones you wanted to be guilty--two REALLY bad guys--lose an eye and gets his face burnt off, apparently without too many aftereffects or problems. They go out in public and live their lives as if nothing happened. Must've been a great surgery for the guy who lost his eye, though the guy who did it was never a doctor or surgeon, or in any health-related field at all.<br /><br />And who was that body in the hospital all that time? Not who you think, but considering how Phantom ended, you couldn't be blamed for not knowing. Turns out, a character from that book hadn't died after all! How could the reader have known? Well, you couldn't, but that's the way it is, anyway.<br /><br />And where's the REALLY, REALLY bad guy everyone spends most of the book looking for? Nobody ever says. Wait for the sequel, I guess. The only intriguing character is a very beautiful, and very unbalanced (Isn't that always the way?) young woman who does something very touching--and out of character--at the end. You won't believe it, just like I didn't.<br /><br />Very cheap. Very lazy.<br /><br />And really disappointing, because I like the series and I like the writer. In fact, I was just thinking of incorporating a technique of his that he uses at the end of every book--what some writers have called his "set pieces," which they essentially are, in a play kind of way. I now realize that these have to be exquisitely staged and described because a) they end every book; b) they're the resolution of the action / mystery / who-dun-it? / police procedural; and c) they're actually the climax, if you combine them with the next book, which I realize is how Nesbo actually writes these. So they serve a ton of functions.<br /><br />But, because of this, they have to be perfect. Great when they are, as most of them have been. Really bad when they're not. And when you combine that with everything I've described above, and throw in a lousy editing job (this could've easily been a few hundred pages shorter), you have a real clunker.<br /><br />And what he did to that recurring female character--chopped her up into many pieces, without mentioning how important she'd been to the series, or her now-orphaned young son--and throw in the fact that she was apparently alive during most of the chopping up...Indefensibly awful.<br /><br />So bad I'm driven by it to work on my own book, and to treat my characters much better. Bad things will still happen to them, but they won't be (or remain) unexplained. And I'll treat them, as I hope I always have, with much more respect.<br /><br />So frustrating because, again, Nesbo is a good writer, and though the tricks in this book are cheap, they work because you turn the pages. You want to figure everything out. You want to see what happens. You want to see it all unravel. And in that sense this book isn't awful, exactly, because I read its 550 hardcover pages in about 24 hours or so.<br /><br />And I'll read the next one.<br /><br />But...<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="4754554825678305738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789164204127" href="/book/show/18088793-polis">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5935491-tanja-berg?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5935491-tanja-berg?shelf=murder-mystery">murder-mystery</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer649650541" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9174349588825575918">4* out of 5. Reviewing a book I read in Swedish by a Norwegian author in English feels silly, but I'm doing it anyway. It will be translated before long. I can't remember the last time I have been so impressed by a crime novel. *draws a blank* I am particularly surprised at how impressed I am because I wasn't really a Jo Nesbø fan. He just wrote mildly entertaining novels one notch above mediocre and is the most famous author in the country I live in, so of course I have to read him. But this, t</span>
  <span id="freeText9174349588825575918" style="display:none">4* out of 5. Reviewing a book I read in Swedish by a Norwegian author in English feels silly, but I'm doing it anyway. It will be translated before long. I can't remember the last time I have been so impressed by a crime novel. *draws a blank* I am particularly surprised at how impressed I am because I wasn't really a Jo Nesbø fan. He just wrote mildly entertaining novels one notch above mediocre and is the most famous author in the country I live in, so of course I have to read him. But this, this was something else.<br /><br />Oh, I don't like Harry Hole, the anti-hero investigator either. Didn't until now that is. He was just too seriously mired in his own problems - his smoking habit, his alcoholism and women trouble. So the fact that he was shot at the end of the last book and appears to be in a coma, well, that was a nice touch. Get him out of the way. And then I can't really say anything more, or I'll be revealing spoilers. There are some truly shocking events within the first 200 pages of this book.<br /><br />Someone is killing police officers. Police officers involved in unsolved murders. These officers are killed in a similar manner, at the same place as the victims. The head of police, Mikael Bellman, is heading into trouble since he cannot solve these new crimes either. <br /><br />After I finished this breathtaking rollercoaster ride I was so caught up in the excitement I did not even notice that there were a few lose plot threads, mostly caused by various red herrings. I'm deducting a star for those. In truth though, I couldn't care less. This was a page-turner, a nail-biter and one hell of a ride like nothing I have experienced for a long, long time. Almost always there's a "meh" part in a book. Usually several. In this book, there wasn't a single one. A+ for entertainment, that's for sure.</span>

<div id="review_789494511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Mal Warwick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4739424-mal-warwick"><img alt="Mal Warwick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294014688p2/4739424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/789494511?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mal Warwick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mal Warwick" href="/user/show/4739424-mal-warwick">Mal Warwick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4739424-mal-warwick?shelf=mysteries-thrillers">mysteries-thrillers</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer789494511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4223094362697358079">What is it about Scandinavian thriller writers? Is it just that they’ve got nothing better to do on all those cold nights than dream up more and more diabolical means to mislead readers? It’s tempting to think so.<br/><br/>Among the many other things he’s done in his still-young life, Jo Nesbo has written ten novels featuring the exasperating Oslo police detective Harry Hole. Inspector Hole is, not to put too fine an edge on it, a piece of work. An alcoholic, deeply anti-authoritarian, and an obsessive in</span>
  <span id="freeText4223094362697358079" style="display:none">What is it about Scandinavian thriller writers? Is it just that they’ve got nothing better to do on all those cold nights than dream up more and more diabolical means to mislead readers? It’s tempting to think so.<br /><br />Among the many other things he’s done in his still-young life, Jo Nesbo has written ten novels featuring the exasperating Oslo police detective Harry Hole. Inspector Hole is, not to put too fine an edge on it, a piece of work. An alcoholic, deeply anti-authoritarian, and an obsessive investigator, he has finally cashed in all his chips with the department as Police opens.<br /><br />Harry Hole is now an ex-policeman, employed as a lecturer at the police academy. His nemesis, a younger detective whose corrupt involvement in the drug trade Harry has uncovered but can’t prove, has just been named Chief of Police. Now someone starts murdering police officers, and doing so at the sites of previous, unsolved murders. Harry’s old colleagues on the force become desperate as the murders continue. The pressure on Harry to come out of retirement becomes fierce.<br /><br />Reviewers use words like “compelling” and “dizzying” and “relentless” to describe the tension that builds in stories like these. Despite knowing that I was being manipulated by a master storyteller, I found myself hooked. On several occasions as I read Police I looked up at the end of a chapter, only to discover that I’d read not one but three chapters and made myself late for something else. Is this addiction? Maybe it is.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4223094362697358079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_741957189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Luanne Ollivier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1621569-luanne-ollivier"><img alt="Luanne Ollivier" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300834900p2/1621569.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/741957189?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luanne Ollivier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luanne Ollivier" href="/user/show/1621569-luanne-ollivier">Luanne Ollivier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846555961" href="/book/show/16134936-police">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer741957189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6024350938569323792">Jo Nesbo left us wondering at the end of the ninth book (Phantom) in his Detective Harry Hole series if there would be a tenth book. There is indeed - Police. I think it's the best one yet.<br/><br/> Quite frankly, it's one of the best detective stories I've read in a long time. Nesbo's plotting is spectacular. I really had no idea where the book was going to go. Suspects abound and deceit, lies and corruption are the order of the day from everyone - criminals and cops.<br/><br/> A mysterious unnamed man in a coma </span>
  <span id="freeText6024350938569323792" style="display:none">Jo Nesbo left us wondering at the end of the ninth book (Phantom) in his Detective Harry Hole series if there would be a tenth book. There is indeed - Police. I think it's the best one yet.<br /><br /> Quite frankly, it's one of the best detective stories I've read in a long time. Nesbo's plotting is spectacular. I really had no idea where the book was going to go. Suspects abound and deceit, lies and corruption are the order of the day from everyone - criminals and cops.<br /><br /> A mysterious unnamed man in a coma being guarded around the clock in the hospital. Who is he? Why is he so important? Police officers are being killed on the scenes of old unsolved crimes - ones that they were involved in. necessarily solved. How is someone getting the drop on a police officer? And Harry's old unit?Disbanded. Where is Harry?<br /><br /> Oh, Nesbo is so clever with his storytelling! I was hooked from the first page to the very last (and very happy that there were 500 delicious pages to enjoy!) The plot is serpentine with another and then another twist slowly added, entangling the reader. Police is dark<br /><br /> Harry Hole is one of the most tortured, conflicted, complicated protagonists in crime fiction. Police finds him in a different place, both physically and mentally. But is it a better place? Hole continues to fight demons both within and without, walking a fine line between chasing criminals and becoming one. <br /><br /> Police is a brilliantly dark read. And just when the story is winding down and you thought you could take a deep breath - Nesbo snatches it away again in the final pages with another gut wrenching ending that will have fans counting down the days 'til the next entry in this fantastic series. <br /><br /> I have Jo Nesbo and Harry Hole on my must read list. Nesbo combines fantastic characters, great plotting, lots of action and suspense and yes, social commentary into addictive reads. Although you could pick up Police and dive into the series, I think new readers of this series need to start with an earlier book to fully appreciate Harry.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6024350938569323792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('03GEMRJmmjbAHtwrcsk/8TddLQWWkzHSEfcEwaUkur8O7kqrut2P7Yiy4h0gC/tODuQwdvIt+l1VfYN3bxOfeg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }
